## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t). Nonlinear oscillators extend the simple harmonic case with higher-order position terms, nonlinear damping, and parametric effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping + Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (combined nonlinearities)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity / asymmetric potential)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric + cubic restoring)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation; even powers (x²) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation (damping) or injection (negative damping/self-excitation)
- Terms like (1 - c*x²)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of limit cycle oscillators (Van der Pol type)
- Explicit time dependence through sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Product terms x*v suggest phase-space-dependent forces or coordinate-velocity coupling in nonlinear systems
- Cubic velocity terms v³ indicate nonlinear drag forces common in fluid-coupled oscillators
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling between x and periodic functions of t (e.g., x*cos(c*t))
- The sign of the cubic coefficient relative to the linear term determines hardening (same sign restoring) vs softening (opposite sign) spring behavior
- Absence of explicit t-dependence indicates an autonomous system where energy is conserved or dissipated but not externally driven

- `v` term: `-0.424310587218182*v`

- `sin(t)` term: `+0.30645527626767*sin(t)`
